    "headers" : {
      "type" : "object",
      "description" : "Initial name + value pairs of the message. Cannot be changed during pipeline processing. Only strings are allowed as values. Optional.",
      "properties" : {
        "name" : {
          "type" : "string",
          "description" : "The name of this pipeline (optional)."
        },
        "description" : {
          "type" : "string",
          "description" : "The description of this pipeline (optional)."
        },
        "runAs" : {
          "type" : "string",
          "description" : "Deprecated. Use Command iam.run.as or Authorization header instead. A username in the format username:USERNAME or uuid in the format uuid:UUID of a user under which this pipeline must be executed as. If not set, runs as the currently logged-in user."
        },
        "onCommandError" : {
          "type" : "string",
          "description" : "Optional value to define what should happen if a command in this pipeline caused an error. Possible values are: IGNORE (Error is logged as warning, further execution of pipeline is not stopped). LOG (The full stacktrace of the exception is logged as error, but no exception is thrown, so next command in pipeline will be executed). THROW (The exception is thrown and the pipeline execution is stopped at this command. This is the default behavior in case this header doesnt exist or is empty). RETRY; times=1, wait=3; then=THROW; (If command caused an error, the command is again executed. Can be parameterized with: times (the number of times to retry before giving up, default=1), wait (the wait time in seconds between two retries, default = 3), then (what to do if it failed after retries. Possible values are IGNORE, LOG, THROW)."
        },
        "exprPrefix" : {
          "type" : "string",
          "description" : "Changes the default prefix # of PEL expressions. Default: #"
        },
        "apiVersion" : {
          "type" : "string",
          "description" : "Defines the version of the commands API to be used. Default: latest"
        },
        "apitoken" : {
          "type" : "string",
          "description" : "The apitoken to be used for authentication. Optional."
        },
        "username" : {
          "type" : "string",
          "description" : "The username to be used for authentication. Note: The use of this header is discouraged. Prefer header apitoken instead. Optional."
        },
        "password" : {
          "type" : "string",
          "description" : "The password to be used for authentication. Note: The use of this header is discouraged. Prefer header apitoken instead. Optional."
        }
      }

In order to find out whether current iteration index is odd or even, use `vars.loop.[as].even`. Whereas [as] stands for the name given by the [as] parameter. Note: Even if not an error, you should prefer to set the `as` parameter for every `foreach` command. Not using it is discouraged and support for not using it will be removed in future versions.",

                "default" : "loop"
              },
              "as" : {
                "type" : "string",
                "description" : "For each iteration/split, puts the current iteration item into the vars scope under this name. If this parameter is null or empty, the item wont be additionally exposed to vars scope. Additionally puts the current loop context under the variable name `vars.loop.NAME.item` whereas `NAME` is the value of this `as` parameter. For example, if you set `as` to `myitem`, then you can access the item using the path `vars.loop.myitem.item` or `vars.myitem`.The loop context contains these objects for each iteration: `item` = The current iteration item. In case the iteration input is a map or a JSON, you can access the key of the item using `item.key` and the value using `item.value`.`index` = The current 0-based iteration index. `even` = A boolean value whether current iteration index is even or not. This is useful for example for layouting."

          "mail.verify" : {
            "type" : "object",
            "description" : " Protects any subsequent pipe commands: Pipeline is only executed \n in case the caller has verified that he is the owner of given \n email address. To do so, a magic link (verification link) is sent \n to his email account. Only if the user clicks on this link within \n a certain amount of time (default is 10min), the subsequent pipe \n commands are executed. From a technical point of view this is done \n by putting the current state of the message into a cache which deletes \n any entries older than 10min. Then, the email with the key to this \n cache entry (=challenge) is send to the user. If the user clicks on \n this link, the message is loaded from the cache using the challenge as \n the key. If the user clicked within 10min, the entry is here, can be \n loaded and the message execution can be resumed. Otherwise if the user \n clicks after 10min on the link, no more entry in it.
